Tutorial 06: Using Requests and Regular Expressions to Count Words¶

Here we use the requests library to actually grab web data from Wikipedia as an HTML page. Using the regular expressions you saw in the prior tutorial, you'll remove all of the special formatting and count the most frequent words found on the page. This will be our first chance to do something with the actual data from Wikipedia.

Modules¶

To start, we will load both the re module and the requests module. The second is what we will use to extract websites into Python.

In [1]:
import re
import requests

Making a request¶

We will start by all grabbing the Wikipedia webpage associated with the University of Richmond. At the end of the tutorial, you'll be able to grab a website of your own choosing. I suggest opening the Wikipedia page in another tab so that you can compare the website with the extracted code in Python.

To make a "request" using the requests module, we use the function get and pass it the full URL to the page, like this:

In [2]:
url = 'https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Richmond'
r = requests.get(url)
r
Out[2]:
<Response [200]>

You'll notice that the object that is returned, called r here, does not print out anything resembling the actual website. Instead, we just get a message that should say <Response [200]> (if not, you have a problem; perhaps a network connectivity issue). What this means is that the request was processed and returned the HTTP status code of 200. This indicates that the request was processed with a status of OK; more verbosely:

Standard response for successful HTTP requests. The actual response will depend on the request method used. In a GET request, the response will contain an entity corresponding to the requested resource. In a POST request, the response will contain an entity describing or containing the result of the action.

The response given by the website contains a number of elements. For example, there is the "HTTP header" that contains metadata about the HTTP request:

In [3]:
r.headers
Out[3]:
{'Date': 'Mon, 17 Sep 2018 17:52:57 GMT', 'Content-Type': 'text/html; charset=UTF-8', 'Content-Length': '36306', 'Connection': 'keep-alive', 'Server': 'mw2185.codfw.wmnet', 'Vary': 'Accept-Encoding,Cookie,Authorization', 'X-Content-Type-Options': 'nosniff', 'P3P': 'CP="This is not a P3P policy! See https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:CentralAutoLogin/P3P for more info."', 'X-Powered-By': 'HHVM/3.18.6-dev', 'Content-language': 'en', 'Last-Modified': 'Fri, 14 Sep 2018 04:35:15 GMT', 'Backend-Timing': 'D=77933 t=1537075688412018', 'Content-Encoding': 'gzip', 'X-Varnish': '494438068 480502942, 1028809545 786386612', 'Via': '1.1 varnish (Varnish/5.1), 1.1 varnish (Varnish/5.1)', 'Age': '31107', 'X-Cache': 'cp2016 hit/1, cp2004 hit/13', 'X-Cache-Status': 'hit-front', 'Strict-Transport-Security': 'max-age=106384710; includeSubDomains; preload', 'Set-Cookie': 'WMF-Last-Access=17-Sep-2018;Path=/;HttpOnly;secure;Expires=Fri, 19 Oct 2018 12:00:00 GMT, WMF-Last-Access-Global=17-Sep-2018;Path=/;Domain=.wikipedia.org;HttpOnly;secure;Expires=Fri, 19 Oct 2018 12:00:00 GMT, GeoIP=US:VA:Richmond:37.58:-77.53:v4; Path=/; secure; Domain=.wikipedia.org', 'X-Analytics': 'ns=0;page_id=856511;https=1;nocookies=1', 'X-Client-IP': '141.166.146.150', 'Cache-Control': 'private, s-maxage=0, max-age=0, must-revalidate', 'Accept-Ranges': 'bytes'}

The part that we are most interested in, however, is the text of the response. This is given by the attribute text, which we can print out as follows:

In [4]:
print(r.text)

<p>The <b>University of Richmond</b> (<b>UR</b> or <b>U of R</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Private_school" title="Private school">private</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nonsectarian" title="Nonsectarian">nonsectarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal arts">liberal arts</a> <a href="/wiki/College" title="College">college</a> located in the city of <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, with small portions of the campus extending into surrounding <a href="/wiki/Henrico_County,_Virginia" title="Henrico County, Virginia">Henrico County</a>.  University of Richmond is a primarily undergraduate, residential university with approximately 4,350 undergraduate and graduate students in five schools: the School of Arts and Sciences, the <a href="/wiki/E._Claiborne_Robins_School_of_Business" title="E. Claiborne Robins School of Business">E. Claiborne Robins School of Business</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jepson_School_of_Leadership_Studies" title="Jepson School of Leadership Studies">Jepson School of Leadership Studies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond_School_of_Law" title="University of Richmond School of Law">University of Richmond School of Law</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond_School_of_Professional_%26_Continuing_Studies" title="University of Richmond School of Professional &amp; Continuing Studies">School of Professional &amp; Continuing Studies</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Founded by Virginia <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> in 1830 as a manual labor institute for men wishing to become ministers, with instruction begun by the Rev. Edward Baptist, an 1813 graduate of <a href="/wiki/Hampden%E2%80%93Sydney_College" title="Hampden–Sydney College">Hampden–Sydney College</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> the school was incorporated ten years later as <b>Richmond College</b>.  After 1834, the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Columbia (Richmond, Virginia)">Columbia House</a> was the main academic building of Richmond College.<sup id="cite_ref-VAnom_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VAnom-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, the entire student body formed a regiment and joined the Confederate army. Richmond College's buildings were used as a hospital for <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate</a> troops and later as a <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a> <a href="/wiki/Barracks" title="Barracks">barracks</a>. The college invested all of its funds in Confederate war bonds, and the outcome of the war left it bankrupt.  In 1866, James Thomas donated $5,000 to reopen the college.  The T.C. Williams School of Law opened in 1870.
</p><p>In 1894, the college elected Dr. <a href="/wiki/Frederic_W._Boatwright" title="Frederic W. Boatwright">Frederic W. Boatwright</a> president.  President Boatwright would serve for 51 years.  He is most remembered for raising the funds needed to move the college in 1914 from its original downtown location to a new 350-acre campus in what is now <a href="/wiki/The_West_End_(Richmond,_Virginia)" class="mw-redirect" title="The West End (Richmond, Virginia)">Westhampton</a> area of Richmond, and in doing so created Westhampton College for women.
</p><p>The university's main library, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Boatwright_Memorial_Library&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Boatwright Memorial Library (page does not exist)">Boatwright Memorial Library</a>, is named in Boatwright's honor. Symbolically, the library and its soaring academic gothic tower occupy the highest spot on the grounds. Its grounds were landscaped in 1913, by <a href="/wiki/Warren_H._Manning" title="Warren H. Manning">Warren H. Manning</a> under the supervision of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Gillette" title="Charles Gillette">Charles Gillette</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The institution was renamed <i>University of Richmond</i> in 1920 with the men's college renamed <i>Richmond College</i>.  The distinction of colleges was phased out in the late 20th century, but the respective parts of the campus continue to be referred to as the Westhampton and the Richmond "sides".<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Richmond-Rummell_View.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Richmond-Rummell_View.jpg/250px-Richmond-Rummell_View.jpg" width="250" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Richmond-Rummell_View.jpg/375px-Richmond-Rummell_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Richmond-Rummell_View.jpg/500px-Richmond-Rummell_View.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="910" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Richmond-Rummell_View.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Richmond College" in 1915, shortly after the transition to Richmond's West End. Rummell, Richard (1848-1924).<sup id="cite_ref-http&#58;//grahamarader.blogspot.com/2011/07/college-view-of-day-richmond-college.html_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http://grahamarader.blogspot.com/2011/07/college-view-of-day-richmond-college.html-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In 1949, the E. Claiborne Robins School of Business opened, followed by the School of Continuing Studies in 1962. In 1969, when financial issues threatened closing the university or turning it over to the Commonwealth of Virginia, <a href="/wiki/E._Claiborne_Robins_Sr" title="E. Claiborne Robins Sr">E. Claiborne Robins Sr</a>., a <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">trustee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alumnus" title="Alumnus">alumnus</a>, donated $50 million to the university, the largest gift made to an institution of higher education at the time. In constant dollars, it remains among the largest. Robins' goal was to make Richmond one of the best private universities in the country. In partnership with the university's president <a href="/wiki/E._Bruce_Heilman" title="E. Bruce Heilman">E. Bruce Heilman</a> and development director <a href="/wiki/H._Gerald_Quigg" title="H. Gerald Quigg">H. Gerald Quigg</a> the $10 million matching grant component of the gift raised over an additional $60 million, making the university's total endowment at the time one of the highest in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Richmond was one of 131 colleges and universities nationally that took part in the <a href="/wiki/V-12_Navy_College_Training_Program" title="V-12 Navy College Training Program">V-12 Navy College Training Program</a> which offered students a path to a Navy commission.<sup id="cite_ref-richmond-v-12_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richmond-v-12-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1987, a donation of $20 million by Robert S. Jepson, Jr. facilitated the opening of the Jepson School of Leadership Studies.<sup id="cite_ref-Jepson_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jepson-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The school, which opened in 1992, was the first of its kind in the U.S.
</p><p>In 1990, the academic missions of Richmond and Westhampton Colleges were combined to form the School of Arts and Sciences.
</p><p>On October 15, 1992, candidates <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ross_Perot" title="Ross Perot">Ross Perot</a> came to campus for the first-ever "town hall" televised presidential debate, viewed by 200 million people worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Addressing a crowd of nearly 9,000, <a href="/wiki/President_Obama" class="mw-redirect" title="President Obama">President Obama</a> visited the University of Richmond to present the <a href="/wiki/American_Jobs_Act" title="American Jobs Act">American Jobs Act</a> on September 11, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dr. Ronald A. Crutcher is the current president of the University of Richmond, becoming the 10th president on July 1, 2015. He is a former member of the Cincinnati Symphony Orchestra.  He is recognized to be the first cellist to receive the doctor of musical arts degree from Yale, where he also earned his master's degree.
</p><p>On, February 23, 2015, the University of Richmond announced to the student body via email that the board of trustees elected <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Crutcher" title="Ronald Crutcher">Ronald Crutcher</a> as the 10th president of the university. He took office 1 July 2015, and his inauguration ceremony was held at the Robins Center on 30 October 2015.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Henry_Mansfield_Cannon_Memorial_Chapel" title="Henry Mansfield Cannon Memorial Chapel">Henry Mansfield Cannon Memorial Chapel</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Court" title="North Court">North Court</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ryland_Hall_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Ryland Hall (Richmond, Virginia)">Ryland Hall</a> were listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-nps_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nps-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="School_of_Arts_.26_Sciences"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Arts_&amp;_Sciences">School of Arts &amp; Sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: School of Arts &amp; Sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>All Richmond undergraduate students begin their course work in the School of Arts &amp; Sciences (A&amp;S), which offers 38 majors and 10 concentrations in the arts, sciences, social sciences, and humanities.  After one full year of study, students may decide to pursue majors in the other undergraduate schools, though 70 percent of students choose to remain in A&amp;S.
</p><p>Opportunities abound in the School of Art &amp; Sciences, as students have the chance to study abroad and pursue internships or research while gaining an education that will prepare them for a variety of careers or graduate programs.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Robins_School_of_Business">Robins School of Business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Robins School of Business">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/E._Claiborne_Robins_School_of_Business" title="E. Claiborne Robins School of Business">E. Claiborne Robins School of Business</a></div>
<p>The Robins School of Business was established in 1949 and offers undergraduate, graduate and executive education programs. It is named after alumnus E. Claiborne Robins.
</p><p>Ranked 12th nationally overall and tied for first in academic quality by <i>BusinessWeek</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-BW_undergrad_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BW_undergrad-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> the Robins School is the only fully accredited, top-ranked undergraduate business school that also is part of a top-ranked liberal arts university.  In the 2009 <i>BusinessWeek</i> review of part-time MBA programs, the Robins school ranked 3rd in the mid-Atlantic region and 17th nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-BW_MBA_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BW_MBA-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Admission into the Robins School of Business is granted to students who have completed basic Accounting, Economics and Math courses at the end of three semester while maintaining a Grade Point Average of 2.7 or higher.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jepson_School_of_Leadership_Studies">Jepson School of Leadership Studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Jepson School of Leadership Studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jepson_School_of_Leadership_Studies" title="Jepson School of Leadership Studies">Jepson School of Leadership Studies</a></div>
<p>The Jepson School of <a href="/wiki/Leadership_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="Leadership Studies">Leadership Studies</a> was founded to address a perceived need in the modern world for the academic study of leadership. The school blends a curriculum of economics, history, literature, philosophy, politics, psychology and religion so that students can learn conceptual tools that support the exercise of leadership in varied settings. As of 2016, the Jepson School remains as the only school of its kind in the United States that is completely devoted to the study of leadership.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Law">School of Law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: School of Law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond_School_of_Law" title="University of Richmond School of Law">University of Richmond School of Law</a></div>
<p>Chartered in 1840, Richmond College was only 30 years old when it added a Law Department. The initial years were very successful for the new Law Department but during the difficult financial times that followed the Civil War, legal education was intermittent at Richmond College until 1890. In that year, the family of the late T.C. Williams, Sr., endowed a Professorship of Law, thus assuring the continuous teaching of law at Richmond College. The law school was granted membership in the Association of American Law Schools in 1930 and now enrolls approximately 500 full-time students and has 4,300 active alumni.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_of_Professional_and_Continuing_Studies">School of Professional and Continuing Studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: School of Professional and Continuing Studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The School of Professional and Continuing Studies offers degree and certificate programs, enrichment opportunities, professional training, and college course work for part-time and non-traditional students of all ages. A variety of evening programs with credit and non-credit courses make it possible for those with busy schedules to further their education or explore new interests.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_academics">Undergraduate academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Undergraduate academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BoatwrightTower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/BoatwrightTower.jpg/250px-BoatwrightTower.jpg" width="250" height="333" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/BoatwrightTower.jpg/375px-BoatwrightTower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/BoatwrightTower.jpg/500px-BoatwrightTower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="2272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BoatwrightTower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boatwright Memorial Library bell tower</div></div></div>
<p>All students must complete general education requirements as part of the liberal arts curriculum.  These requirements include a freshman seminar that all first-year students must complete. Other general education requirements include expository writing, wellness, foreign language, and one class each in six fields of study.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Richmond offers more than 100 majors, minors, and concentrations in three undergraduate schools—the School of Arts and Sciences, the  Robins School of Business, and the Jepson School of Leadership Studies.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The School of Continuing Studies, primarily an evening school focused on part-time adult students, offers additional degree programs in selected areas.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Richmond admitted 31.1 percent of applicants for the class of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-admissions.richmond.edu_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admissions.richmond.edu-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The 811-member class of 2019 has a middle 50 percent range for SAT scores of 1975-2180 and a middle 50 percent range for ACT scores of 30-33.<sup id="cite_ref-admissions.richmond.edu_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admissions.richmond.edu-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In its "America's Best Colleges 2014" issue, <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> ranked Richmond 25th among national liberal arts colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> also ranked Richmond second among "up-and-coming" liberal arts colleges,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and as the 9th best value among national liberal arts colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Kiplinger ranked Richmond 11th among the "Best Private Colleges" in the U.S. for 2013, leaving three Ivy League Universities behind in the top 20.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Richmond was ranked 8th by <i><a href="/wiki/SmartMoney" title="SmartMoney">SmartMoney</a></i> in the category "Best Private Colleges of 2011", leaving two Ivy League Universities behind in the top 10.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect" title="BusinessWeek">BusinessWeek</a></i> ranked the E. Claiborne Robins School of Business as the 12th best undergraduate program in the nation in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-BW_undergrad_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BW_undergrad-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The Princeton Review named Richmond No. 14 for Financial Aid, No. 13 for Best Career Services and No. 17 for Most Beautiful Campus in its 2013 edition of "The Best 376 Colleges".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Time magazine's Money section named Richmond among "the top 10 colleges with the most generous financial aid."<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, Richmond was ranked as the 18th best liberal arts college in America by Niche.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The University of Richmond's name leads some to believe that it is a public institution drawing students primarily from within Virginia. However, only about 15 percent of UR's undergraduate students are from Virginia.<sup id="cite_ref-Geographic_Distribution_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geographic_Distribution-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The University of Richmond draws many students from the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Mid-Atlantic States">Mid-Atlantic</a> regions of the United States, but also from across the country and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-Geographic_Distribution_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geographic_Distribution-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_aid">Financial aid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Financial aid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Richmond administers a generous <a href="/wiki/Student_financial_aid_(United_States)" title="Student financial aid (United States)">financial aid</a> program, with more than 60 percent of all students receiving some form of financial assistance.  Richmond offers a <a href="/wiki/Need-blind_admission" title="Need-blind admission">need-blind</a> admissions policy that does not consider an applicant's ability to pay in the admission decision, and it pledges to meet 100 percent of an admitted domestic student's demonstrated need.  Richmond also offers 50 merit-based, full tuition scholarships to students in each entering class (approximately 1 out of every 15 students).  Richmond also caps student loan debt depending on the year of the student.  A senior has the highest cap at $7,500 per year, whereas a freshman cannot take a loan more than $5,500.  Recently, to encourage enrollment from Virginia residents, admitted students from Virginia with family incomes of $60,000 or less receive full-tuition/room and board financial aid packages without loans. Richmond's financial aid program is due, in no small part, to its endowment of over $2 billion, placing it within the top 40 nationally among college and university endowments.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_research">Student research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Student research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Richmond offers numerous research opportunities for students. In addition to research-based courses, independent studies, and practicums in most disciplines, many special opportunities exist for students to participate in close research collaborations with faculty. Student research occurs in all academic areas, including the arts, sciences, social sciences, and other fields.  Notably, the university recently received a $1.5 million grant from the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> for its mathematics program to sponsor student research commencing May 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The University of Richmond is listed in <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. News and World Report">U.S. News and World Report</a>'s</i> "America's Best Colleges 2008" issue as one of 35 (out of 2,500) "schools with outstanding examples of academic programs that are believed to lead to student success" in the area of "undergraduate research/creative projects."<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Richmond has over 165 student organizations.  Student groups include those devoted to:
</p>
<ul><li>Academic interests: (<a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Kappa" title="Phi Beta Kappa">Phi Beta Kappa</a>; WILL*, formerly Women Involved in Learning and Living; <a href="/wiki/Model_United_Nations" title="Model United Nations">Model United Nations</a>),</li>
<li>Student government: (Richmond College Student Government Association and Westhampton College Government Association)</li>
<li>Media: <i>The Collegian</i>, student newspaper published since 1914; <i>Forum Magazine</i>, a student magazine published in 2013; <i>WDCE</i>, campus radio station; <i>The Messenger</i>, annual arts and literary magazine);</li>
<li>Community service: (<a href="/wiki/Bonner_Scholars" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonner Scholars">Bonner Scholars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habitat_for_Humanity" title="Habitat for Humanity">Habitat for Humanity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Omega" title="Alpha Phi Omega">Alpha Phi Omega</a>, Volunteer Action Council (VAC)),</li>
<li>Club sports: (Richmond Crew, Richmond Ice Hockey Club, Richmond Men's and Women's Soccer, Richmond Co-Ed Swimming, Richmond Synchronized Swimming, Richmond Quidditch, Ultimate Frisbee Club, Richmond Archery Club <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Spiders#Rugby" title="Richmond Spiders">University of Richmond Rugby Football Club</a>)</li>
<li>Religion: <a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond_Office_of_the_Chaplaincy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="University of Richmond Office of the Chaplaincy (page does not exist)">The Office of the Chaplaincy</a> is home to 18 different campus ministries and hosts many different services and events for staff, faculty, and students.  The mission of the Office of the Chaplaincy is to "Inspire generous faith and engage the heart of the University." <sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Performing arts: (including four <a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a> groups: The Octāves, Choeur du Roi, The Sirens, and Off The Cuff; and a student run Improv Comedy Troupe, Subject to Change, which performs free shows on campus several times a year and has also performed at festivals across the mid-Atlantic)</li>
<li>Culture and diversity: (Ngoma African Dance Company, Multicultural Student Union, SCOPE for the LGBTQ+ community, Russian and Slavic Cultural Organization, Cultural Advisors)</li></ul>
<p>Richmond also has an active Greek life with 15 national fraternities and sororities.  The fraternities include <a href="/wiki/Theta_Chi" title="Theta Chi">Theta Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Alpha" title="Alpha Phi Alpha">Alpha Phi Alpha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Order" title="Kappa Alpha Order">Kappa Alpha Order</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Gamma_Delta" title="Phi Gamma Delta">Phi Gamma Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Chi_Alpha" title="Lambda Chi Alpha">Lambda Chi Alpha</a> and the founding chapter of <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Phi_Epsilon" title="Sigma Phi Epsilon">Sigma Phi Epsilon</a>. The Upsilon Gamma chapter of <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Alpha" title="Alpha Phi Alpha">Alpha Phi Alpha</a> was the first historically black fraternity to be chartered on Richmond's campus. The sororities are <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Alpha" title="Alpha Kappa Alpha">Alpha Kappa Alpha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Sigma_Theta" title="Delta Sigma Theta">Delta Sigma Theta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Delta_Delta" title="Delta Delta Delta">Delta Delta Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Gamma" title="Delta Gamma">Delta Gamma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Delta" title="Kappa Delta">Kappa Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Gamma" title="Kappa Kappa Gamma">Kappa Kappa Gamma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pi_Beta_Phi" title="Pi Beta Phi">Pi Beta Phi</a>. About 50 percent of the women and over 30 percent of the men participate in the Greek system.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The University of Richmond is home to one known secret society <a href="/w/index.php?title=RS_(University_of_Richmond)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="RS (University of Richmond) (page does not exist)">RS (University of Richmond)</a>. Made up of Richmond College students, the Society is known for its markings on campus and its dedication to University school spirit and camaraderie.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1990–2003, the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Quartet" title="Shanghai Quartet">Shanghai Quartet</a> served as quartet-in-residence at UR, and their relationship with the university continues with their roles as Distinguished Visiting Artists.  In 2004, contemporary music sextet <a href="/wiki/Eighth_blackbird" class="mw-redirect" title="Eighth blackbird">eighth blackbird</a> (spelled in all lowercase) was named ensemble-in-residence. Camp Concert Hall, located on campus, is a favorite recording venue for <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" class="mw-redirect" title="National Public Radio">National Public Radio</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Noted University of Richmond traditions include: an <a href="/wiki/Honor_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Honor code">honor code</a> administered by student honor councils;<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Investiture and Proclamation Night, ceremonies for first year men and women to reflect on their next four years;<sup id="cite_ref-traditions_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-traditions-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Ring Dance, a dance held at the <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Hotel_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Jefferson Hotel (Richmond, Virginia)">Jefferson Hotel</a> by the junior class women;<sup id="cite_ref-traditions_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-traditions-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and Pig Roast, a large annual event held during the spring semester which draws significant gatherings of current students and alumni to the fraternity lodges and have featured musical acts such as <a href="/wiki/Flo_Rida" title="Flo Rida">Flo Rida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afroman" title="Afroman">Afroman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>  Another long-standing Richmond tradition is the crowning of the largest goose on Westhampton Lake with the title "Triceragoose." This establishes that goose as the king of the lake, ruling over all ducks, geese, and freshmen.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_education">International education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: International education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the past decade, the university has sought to develop a stronger international focus.  International students from about 70 countries represent about 7 percent of the student body.  Approximately half of undergraduate students participate in one of 78 <a href="/wiki/Study_abroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Study abroad">study abroad</a> programs offered by the university.  Other international programs include Global House, a residential program housed in  Keller Hall, and an international film series. In 2014, the Office of International Education at the university created the International Student Advisory Board, a group of students dedicated to working with administration to improve the overall experience of international students on campus. Alumna Carole Weinstein recently donated $9 million toward the construction of a new building on campus, opened in the fall of 2010, dedicated to international education.<sup id="cite_ref-caroleweinstein_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caroleweinstein-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_campus">Main campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Main campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Richmond's campus consists of 350 acres (1.4&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) in a suburban setting on the western edge of the city. Most of the campus lies within the city limits; a small section of the south campus, including the Special Programs Building (home to the student health center and the campus police), intramural sports fields, and most of the campus apartments, lies within Henrico County.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The university has, with few exceptions, remained true to the original architectural plans for the campus—red brick buildings in a <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Collegiate gothic">collegiate gothic</a> style set around shared open lawns.  Many of the original buildings, including Jeter Hall and North Court, both residence halls, and Ryland Hall, the original administration building and library for Richmond College, were designed by <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Adams_Cram" title="Ralph Adams Cram">Ralph Adams Cram</a> in 1910. Cram, a noted institutional architect, also designed buildings for <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice_University" title="Rice University">Rice</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Williams_College" title="Williams College">Williams</a>, among other universities.  <a href="/wiki/Warren_Manning" class="mw-redirect" title="Warren Manning">Warren H. Manning</a>, a former apprentice to <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Law_Olmsted" title="Frederick Law Olmsted">Frederick Law Olmsted</a>, designed the original landscape plan.  The overall effect of the gothic architecture set amid a landscape of pines, rolling hills, and Westhampton Lake, is intimate and tranquil. In 2000, the campus was recognized by <a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a> as the most beautiful in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CommonsLake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/23/CommonsLake.jpg/250px-CommonsLake.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/23/CommonsLake.jpg/375px-CommonsLake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/23/CommonsLake.jpg/500px-CommonsLake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CommonsLake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Looking out over Westhampton Lake from Tyler Haynes Commons</div></div></div>
<p>The University of Richmond campus was used to film portions of the pilot of the ABC TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Commander_in_Chief_(television)" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander in Chief (television)">Commander in Chief</a></i>, and lead character <a href="/wiki/Mackenzie_Allen" class="mw-redirect" title="Mackenzie Allen">Mackenzie Allen</a> (played by <a href="/wiki/Geena_Davis" title="Geena Davis">Geena Davis</a>) served as <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_(education)" title="Chancellor (education)">chancellor</a> of a fictionalized University of Richmond prior to her election as <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President of the United States</a>. Much of the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Cry_Wolf_(2005_film)" title="Cry Wolf (2005 film)">Cry Wolf</a></i> was filmed on the Westhampton side of campus, with several dormitories, including South Court, North Court, and Keller Hall, serving as locations. An episode of the television show <i><a href="/wiki/Dawson%27s_Creek" title="Dawson&#39;s Creek">Dawson's Creek</a></i> was filmed on campus, which served as an unnamed "beautiful Ivy League campus." The filming itself took place in locations throughout the campus, even including rowing on Westhampton Lake.
</p><p>The University of Richmond owns the former <a href="/wiki/Reynolds_Metals_Company_International_Headquarters" title="Reynolds Metals Company International Headquarters">Reynolds Metals Executive Office Building</a>, a gift-purchase from <a href="/wiki/Alcoa" title="Alcoa">Alcoa</a> in 2001.  Located a few miles from campus, the 250,000-square-foot (23,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) building was designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Bunshaft" title="Gordon Bunshaft">Gordon Bunshaft</a> and opened in 1958.  The building, which incorporates nearly 1.4 million pounds of <a href="/wiki/Aluminum" class="mw-redirect" title="Aluminum">aluminum</a>, is listed in the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>.  It currently serves as the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Altria_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Altria Group">Altria Group</a> and its subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Morris_USA" title="Philip Morris USA">Philip Morris USA</a>, which lease it from the university.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>  In early 2001, the university  finalized the purchase of 115 acres (0.47&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of land in eastern <a href="/wiki/Goochland_County,_Virginia" title="Goochland County, Virginia">Goochland County</a>, a few miles from the main campus.  The land is currently used for biology research, but future uses could include intramural athletic fields.<sup id="cite_ref-Goochland_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goochland-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The University of Richmond campus used to be home to the <a href="/wiki/Governor%27s_Schools_(Virginia)#Summer_Residential_Governor&#39;s_Schools" title="Governor&#39;s Schools (Virginia)">Virginia Governor's School for Visual and Performing Arts and Humanities</a> during the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-Governor&#39;s_Schools_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Governor&#39;s_Schools-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UR_Downtown">UR Downtown</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: UR Downtown">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The university also operates UR Downtown, a downtown campus of sorts occupying leased space within a larger building at 626 East Broad street. Despite its small size, UR Downtown hosts the Richmond on Broad café (owned and operated by the university), a mixed-purpose lower-level, art gallery spaces, offices, two classrooms, and a conference room. Located in the city's Arts District, UR Downtown also participates in the monthly art festival, First Fridays. Moreover, the space hosts multiple exhibits each year, often in collaboration with local organizations. The UR Downtown conference room is also home to an original 1956 sgraffito style mural by Hans E. Gassman, created for the bank that occupied the building in the past. Other than art, UR Downtown serves as a VITA site, providing free tax assistance to low-income families. The spaces inside UR Downtown are made available to advocacy and non-profit organizations in need of meeting space. The Caricco Center for Pro Bono law service, the Richmond Families Initiative, and Partners in the Arts also operate out of UR Downtown.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Spiders" title="Richmond Spiders">Richmond Spiders</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Spiders_football" title="Richmond Spiders football">Richmond Spiders football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Spiders_men%27s_basketball" title="Richmond Spiders men&#39;s basketball">Richmond Spiders men's basketball</a></div>
<p>The university won its first national championship in 1982 when women's tennis won the AIAW national championship. The university won its <a href="/wiki/2008_Richmond_Spiders_football_team" title="2008 Richmond Spiders football team">first NCAA national championship</a> in any sport on December 19, 2008, when the Spiders football team defeated the <a href="/wiki/2008_Montana_Grizzlies_football_team" title="2008 Montana Grizzlies football team">Montana Grizzlies</a> 24–7 in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Championship" title="NCAA Division I Football Championship">NCAA Division I Football Championship</a> (which is exclusively for teams in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I#Football_Championship_Subdivision" title="NCAA Division I">Football Championship Subdivision</a>, the second tier of <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">NCAA Division I</a> <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">football</a>).  Richmond was ranked 23rd in men's basketball at one point during the 2009–10 season. During its 2010 season the Richmond Men's Cross Country team placed 24th at the NCAA Division I Cross Country Championships. The <a href="/wiki/2010-11_Richmond_Spiders_men%27s_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="2010-11 Richmond Spiders men&#39;s basketball team">2010-11</a> <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Spiders_men%27s_basketball" title="Richmond Spiders men&#39;s basketball">Richmond Spiders men's basketball</a> team won the <a href="/wiki/2011_Atlantic_10_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2011 Atlantic 10 Men&#39;s Basketball Tournament">2011 Atlantic 10 Men's Basketball Tournament</a>, earning the team a spot in the <a href="/wiki/2011_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 NCAA Men&#39;s Division I Basketball Tournament">2011 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament</a>. The Spiders fell to <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Kansas_Jayhawks_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 Kansas Jayhawks men&#39;s basketball team">Kansas</a> in the Sweet Sixteen.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Richmond_people" title="List of University of Richmond people">List of University of Richmond people</a></div>

The text above is written in a markup language called HTML; rendered in your browser it yields the pretty website that you are used to seeing when you navigate to Wikipedia.

In Python, this text is just stored as a very long string object similar to the strings you saw in Tutorial 3. We will now make use of string methods and regular expression functions to process the string and extract the individual words.

Cleaning HTML code¶

To start, we will save the request text as a variable called website. Just to simplify the processing, in the code below I have also remove the first set of lines corresponding the HTML header and an embedded Javascript chunk at the bottom of the text.

In [5]:
website = r.text
website = website[website.find("<body"):website.find("<noscript>")]
print(website)

<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">University of Richmond</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

<a href="/wiki/File:UR_Shield.svg" class="image"><img alt="UR Shield.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d0/UR_Shield.svg/100px-UR_Shield.svg.png" width="100" height="119" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d0/UR_Shield.svg/150px-UR_Shield.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d0/UR_Shield.svg/200px-UR_Shield.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="91" data-file-height="108" /></a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>University of Richmond</b> (<b>UR</b> or <b>U of R</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Private_school" title="Private school">private</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nonsectarian" title="Nonsectarian">nonsectarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal arts">liberal arts</a> <a href="/wiki/College" title="College">college</a> located in the city of <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, with small portions of the campus extending into surrounding <a href="/wiki/Henrico_County,_Virginia" title="Henrico County, Virginia">Henrico County</a>.  University of Richmond is a primarily undergraduate, residential university with approximately 4,350 undergraduate and graduate students in five schools: the School of Arts and Sciences, the <a href="/wiki/E._Claiborne_Robins_School_of_Business" title="E. Claiborne Robins School of Business">E. Claiborne Robins School of Business</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jepson_School_of_Leadership_Studies" title="Jepson School of Leadership Studies">Jepson School of Leadership Studies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond_School_of_Law" title="University of Richmond School of Law">University of Richmond School of Law</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond_School_of_Professional_%26_Continuing_Studies" title="University of Richmond School of Professional &amp; Continuing Studies">School of Professional &amp; Continuing Studies</a>.
</p>
